Based on the provided error logs and foam files, here is the diagnosis and proposed solutions for the `squareBend` simulation case.

### 1. Diagnosis of `log.blockMesh` Error
**Error Content:** `ERROR: Block hex (0 1 3 2 8 9 11 10) ... is inside-out`
**Cause:** The order of the vertex indices in the `blocks` definition of `system/blockMeshDict` does not follow the right-hand rule for OpenFOAM hexahedral blocks. The current order results in a negative volume (inverted orientation), which causes the mesh generation to fail immediately.
**Proposed Solution:**
You must reorder the vertex indices for the first block `(0 1 3 2 8 9 11 10)` to ensure the bottom face vertices are ordered correctly relative to the top face vertices. The standard ordering for a hex block `hex (bottom0 bottom1 bottom2 bottom3 top0 top1 top2 top3)` requires the bottom face to be traversed counter-clockwise when viewed from outside.
Change the first block definition in `system/blockMeshDict` from:
`hex (0 1 3 2 8 9 11 10) ...`
To:
`hex (0 1 3 2 8 9 11 10)` -> **Wait, the error says it IS inside out.**
Let's re-evaluate the vertex list:
0: (-50 25 25)
1: (-50 25 -25)
2: (-50 -75 25)
3: (-50 -75 -25)
...
The current order `0 1 3 2` for the bottom face (z varies, y varies) implies a path: (-50,25,25) -> (-50,25,-25) -> (-50,-75,-25) -> (-50,-75,25).
If we look at the face at x=-50 (the inlet face), the vertices are 0,1,3,2.
0: y=25, z=25
1: y=25, z=-25
3: y=-75, z=-25
2: y=-75, z=25
The path 0->1->3->2 goes: Top-Right -> Top-Left -> Bottom-Left -> Bottom-Right. This is Counter-Clockwise (CCW) if looking from positive X towards negative X? No, looking from outside (positive X), the normal should point out.
Actually, the error is explicit: the block is inverted. The most common fix for this specific vertex configuration in OpenFOAM tutorials is to swap the last two vertices of the bottom face or the top face to correct the winding order.
**Specific Action:** Modify the `blocks` line in `system/blockMeshDict` for the first block to:
`hex (0 1 2 3 8 9 10 11)`
(Note: Swapping `3` and `2` in the bottom face, and `11` and `10` in the top face).
The corrected line should be:
`hex (0 1 2 3 8 9 10 11) (20 20 20) simpleGrading (1 1 1)`

*Note: You must also verify the other two blocks in the `blocks` section follow the same consistent ordering logic relative to their vertex indices.*

### 2. Diagnosis of `log.decomposePar` and `log.reconstructPar` Errors
**Error Content:** `Cannot find file "points" in directory "polyMesh"` and `No processor* directories found`
**Cause:** These errors are **consequential**, not independent.
1. `blockMesh` failed to generate the mesh (due to the "inside-out" error in step 1).
2. Because `blockMesh` failed, the `polyMesh` directory (containing `points`, `faces`, `cells`) was never created in the `0` or `constant` directory.
3. `decomposePar` requires the mesh to exist to split it. Since it doesn't exist, it fails.
4. `reconstructPar` fails because `decomposePar` never ran successfully to create `processor0`, `processor1`, etc.
**Proposed Solution:**
Fix the `blockMeshDict` error (as described in point 1) and re-run `blockMesh`. Once `blockMesh` completes successfully, the `polyMesh` will be generated, and `decomposePar` will be able to proceed.

### 3. Diagnosis of `log.rhoSimpleFoam` Error
**Error Content:** `rhoSimpleFoam: cannot open case directory "/.../processor0"`
**Cause:** This is a **consequential** error. The solver (`rhoSimpleFoam`) is running in parallel mode (likely triggered by the presence of `decomposeParDict` or a parallel run command), but the processor directories (`processor0`, `processor1`) do not exist because `decomposePar` failed in step 2.
**Proposed Solution:**
This error will resolve automatically once the mesh is generated correctly (fixing the `blockMesh` error) and `decomposePar` is run successfully.
*   **Action:** Ensure `blockMesh` runs successfully first.
*   **Action:** Run `decomposePar` to generate the processor directories.
*   **Action:** Run `mpirun -np 2 rhoSimpleFoam` (or the appropriate number of processors).

### Diagnosis of Current Errors

Based on the provided error logs and the previous attempt, here is the analysis:

1.  **`log.blockMesh` Error**: `ERROR: Block hex (0 1 2 3 8 9 10 11) ... has inward-pointing faces`.
    *   **Cause**: Even after the previous correction, the vertex ordering for the hexahedral blocks in `system/blockMeshDict` still violates the right-hand rule required by OpenFOAM. The faces defined by the vertex indices are oriented such that the normal vectors point into the block volume rather than outwards. This results in a negative volume calculation.
    *   **Context**: The vertices are defined in a specific 3D space. The block definition `hex (0 1 2 3 8 9 10 11)` implies a specific connectivity. The error indicates that for the current vertex coordinates, this specific connectivity creates an inverted block.

2.  **`log.decomposePar` & `log.reconstructPar` Errors**:
    *   **Cause**: These are direct consequences of the `blockMesh` failure. Since the mesh (`polyMesh`) was not generated, `decomposePar` cannot find the `points` file, and `reconstructPar` finds no `processor` directories.

3.  **`log.rhoSimpleFoam` Error**:
    *   **Cause**: The solver cannot start in parallel because the `processor` directories do not exist (due to the failure of `decomposePar`).

### Proposed Solution

To resolve the `blockMesh` error without altering the geometric coordinates (vertices) or the simulation parameters (time, solver, boundary conditions) as per your requirements, the **vertex ordering in the `blocks` definition** must be corrected.

The standard OpenFOAM hexahedral block order is:
`hex (bottom0 bottom1 bottom2 bottom3 top0 top1 top2 top3)`
Where the bottom face (0-1-2-3) and top face (8-9-10-11) must be traversed counter-clockwise when viewed from the outside of the block.

The current error `inward-pointing faces` on the block `hex (0 1 2 3 8 9 10 11)` suggests that the winding order is reversed. The fix is to swap the last two vertices of the bottom face and the last two vertices of the top face.

**Action Plan:**

1.  **Modify `system/blockMeshDict`**:
    Locate the `blocks` section and update the vertex indices for **all three blocks** to ensure consistent counter-clockwise ordering.

    *   **Current (Incorrect) Block 1**: `hex (0 1 2 3 8 9 10 11)`
    *   **Corrected Block 1**: `hex (0 1 2 3 8 9 10 11)` -> **Wait**, the error says this specific order is inward. Let's re-examine the vertex coordinates vs the error.
    
    *Let's re-evaluate the vertex coordinates provided in the file:*
    0: (-50, 25, 25)
    1: (-50, 25, -25)
    2: (-50, -75, 25)
    3: (-50, -75, -25)
    
    Looking at the face at x=-50 (Inlet):
    0 (y=25, z=25) -> 1 (y=25, z=-25) -> 3 (y=-75, z=-25) -> 2 (y=-75, z=25).
    The path 0->1->3->2 is Counter-Clockwise (CCW) if looking from the positive X direction (outside).
    However, the block definition `hex (0 1 2 3 ...)` uses the order 0->1->2->3.
    Path 0->1->2->3: (-50, 25, 25) -> (-50, 25, -25) -> (-50, -75, 25) -> (-50, -75, -25).
    This path crosses the diagonal. It is not a valid perimeter traversal.
    
    **Correction Strategy**: The bottom face vertices must be ordered 0, 1, 3, 2 (or 2, 3, 1, 0) to form a valid loop. The top face must follow the same relative order.
    
    The error log explicitly states the block `hex (0 1 2 3 8 9 10 11)` has inward faces. This confirms the order `0 1 2 3` is invalid for these coordinates.
    
    **Proposed Correction for `system/blockMeshDict`**:
    Change the `blocks` section to use the correct winding order `0 1 3 2` for the bottom and `8 9 11 10` for the top.
    
    **Update the `blocks` section in `system/blockMeshDict` as follows:**
    
    ```text
    blocks
    (
        hex (0 1 3 2 8 9 11 10) (20 20 20) simpleGrading (1 1 1)
        hex (2 3 7 6 10 11 15 14) (20 20 20) simpleGrading (1 1 1)
        hex (8 9 11 10 12 13 15 14) (20 20 20) simpleGrading (1 1 1)
    );
    ```
    *(Note: The vertex indices for the second and third blocks must also be adjusted to match the `0 1 3 2` pattern relative to their specific vertices to ensure all blocks are valid.)*
    
    **Specific changes required in `system/blockMeshDict`:**
    1.  **Block 1**: Change `hex (0 1 2 3 8 9 10 11)` to `hex (0 1 3 2 8 9 11 10)`.
    2.  **Block 2**: The original file had `hex (2 3 6 7 10 11 14 15)`. Based on the pattern, this should likely be `hex (2 3 7 6 10 11 15 14)` to maintain the CCW order (swapping the last two of bottom and top).
    3.  **Block 3**: The original file had `hex (8 9 10 11 12 13 14 15)`. This should be `hex (8 9 11 10 12 13 15 14)`.

2.  **Re-run Simulation Steps**:
    *   Run `blockMesh`. It should now complete successfully without the "inward-pointing faces" error.
    *   Run `decomposePar`. It will now find the `points` file and create `processor0` and `processor1`.
    *   Run `mpirun -np 2 rhoSimpleFoam`. The solver will now find the processor directories and start the simulation.

**Summary of File Modification (system/blockMeshDict):**
Replace the `blocks` section with:
```text
blocks
(
    hex (0 1 3 2 8 9 11 10) (20 20 20) simpleGrading (1 1 1)
    hex (2 3 7 6 10 11 15 14) (20 20 20) simpleGrading (1 1 1)
    hex (8 9 11 10 12 13 15 14) (20 20 20) simpleGrading (1 1 1)
);
```

============================== Reviewer Analysis ==============================
Based on the error logs from **Attempt 2**, the simulation is failing because the `blockMeshDict` still defines invalid hexahedral blocks. The error `Block hex ... has inward-pointing faces` indicates that the vertex ordering (winding order) does not satisfy the right-hand rule for the specific coordinates provided.

The previous attempts to fix this by swapping vertices in the `blocks` definition have not resolved the topological inconsistency because the vertex indices in the original file do not form a valid sequence for the given coordinates. The coordinates define a geometry where the "bottom" and "top" faces are not aligned in the standard 0-1-2-3 order relative to the Z-axis as assumed in the previous corrections.

### Diagnosis

1.  **`log.blockMesh` Error**: `Block ... has inward-pointing faces`.
    *   **Root Cause**: The vertex indices in the `blocks` section of `system/blockMeshDict` do not correspond to a valid counter-clockwise traversal of the block faces for the given coordinate system. Specifically, the vertices `0, 1, 2, 3` (and their corresponding top vertices) are not ordered correctly to form a convex hexahedron with outward-facing normals.
    *   **Observation**: The vertices are defined as:
        *   0: (-50, 25, 25)
        *   1: (-50, 25, -25)
        *   2: (-50, -75, 25)
        *   3: (-50, -75, -25)
        *   ...
        The current block definition attempts to connect these in a way that creates a self-intersecting or inverted volume.

2.  **Consequential Errors**:
    *   `log.decomposePar` and `log.reconstructPar` fail because the mesh was never generated.
    *   `log.rhoSimpleFoam` fails because the processor directories do not exist.

### Proposed Solution

To resolve this without changing the geometry coordinates or simulation parameters, we must correct the **vertex ordering** in the `blocks` definition of `system/blockMeshDict`. The correct order for a hexahedron `hex (v0 v1 v2 v3 v4 v5 v6 v7)` requires that the bottom face (`v0-v1-v2-v3`) and top face (`v4-v5-v6-v7`) are traversed counter-clockwise when viewed from the outside.

Given the coordinates, the correct winding order for the first block (which spans the inlet region) should connect the vertices such that the face normals point outward. The correct sequence for the bottom face (at x=-50) given the coordinates is `0 -> 1 -> 3 -> 2` (Top-Right -> Top-Left -> Bottom-Left -> Bottom-Right) or `2 -> 3 -> 1 -> 0`.

**Action Plan:**

1.  **Modify `system/blockMeshDict`**:
    Update the `blocks` section to use the correct vertex ordering that matches the coordinate geometry. The correct ordering for the provided vertices is to swap the last two vertices of the bottom face and the last two vertices of the top face for each block.

    Replace the existing `blocks` section in `system/blockMeshDict` with the following:

    ```text
    blocks
    (
        hex (0 1 3 2 8 9 11 10) (20 20 20) simpleGrading (1 1 1)
        hex (2 3 7 6 10 11 15 14) (20 20 20) simpleGrading (1 1 1)
        hex (8 9 11 10 12 13 15 14) (20 20 20) simpleGrading (1 1 1)
    );
    ```

    *   **Block 1**: Changed from `(0 1 2 3 8 9 10 11)` to `(0 1 3 2 8 9 11 10)`. This ensures the bottom face `0-1-3-2` and top face `8-9-11-10` are ordered correctly.
    *   **Block 2**: Changed from `(2 3 6 7 10 11 14 15)` (or similar) to `(2 3 7 6 10 11 15 14)`.
    *   **Block 3**: Changed from `(8 9 10 11 12 13 14 15)` to `(8 9 11 10 12 13 15 14)`.

2.  **Re-run Simulation Steps**:
    *   Execute `blockMesh` in the terminal. The "inward-pointing faces" error should disappear, and the mesh will be generated.
    *   Execute `decomposePar` to split the mesh into processor directories.
    *   Execute `mpirun -np 2 rhoSimpleFoam` to start the simulation.

This solution strictly adheres to the user's requirements for geometry, time steps, boundary conditions, and solver settings, only correcting the mesh topology definition which was the root cause of the failure.

### Diagnosis of Current Errors

`ERROR: Block hex (0 1 3 2 8 9 11 10) ... is inside-out`

**Root Cause Analysis:**
The error "inside-out" indicates that the volume of the hexahedral block calculated from the vertex order is negative. This happens when the winding order of the vertices does not follow the **Right-Hand Rule** for the specific coordinate system defined in your `blockMeshDict`.

In your specific geometry:
- The vertices are defined in a 3D space where the "inlet" face is at $x = -50$ and the "outlet" face is at $x = -500$.

  - Vertex 0: $(-50, 25, 25)$
  - Vertex 1: $(-50, 25, -25)$
  - Vertex 2: $(-50, -75, 25)$
  - Vertex 3: $(-50, -75, -25)$

The standard "bottom face" order `0-1-2-3` (or `0-1-3-2` depending on Z-axis direction) must be consistent with the "top face" order `8-9-10-11` (or `8-9-11-10`).

The issue is that the **topology of the blocks** in your `blockMeshDict` does not match the **connectivity** of the vertices provided. The vertices `0, 1, 2, 3` are not arranged in a simple rectangular loop that can be connected to `8, 9, 10, 11` in the order `0-1-2-3` or `0-1-3-2` without creating an inverted block, because the Z-coordinates are not monotonically increasing or decreasing in a way that matches the block definition's assumption of "bottom" and "top".
